## Section 001: Subagent Development Execution Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define the controller, worker, spec-review, quality-review, integration, user-communication, or final-verification responsibilities that make delegation safe
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fresh context reduces contamination, but a worker without complete constraints or an integration owner can produce locally plausible work that conflicts, overbuilds, or passes the wrong tests
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the template overrides a no-commit instruction, workers share files, reports substitute for code inspection, quality review starts before scope is correct, unresolved findings are carried forward, or no one owns cross-task behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference governs same-workspace execution orchestration and does not authorize commits, branches, extra agents, network actions, or scope beyond the user's request
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add explicit controller and worker contracts, dependency-aware dispatch, user-constraint precedence, integration ownership, evidence, and stop rules before preserving seed content
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that delegation improves quality only when the controller retains epistemic and integration responsibility; offloading work is not offloading accountability
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to delegate only a bounded task with explicit inputs, outputs, dependencies, file ownership, permissions, tests, and stop conditions; inspect artifacts through spec review before quality review, then integrate and run final system gates under controller ownership

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference governs same-workspace execution orchestration and does not authorize commits, branches, extra agents, network actions, or scope beyond the user's request
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Subagent Development Execution Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add explicit controller and worker contracts, dependency-aware dispatch, user-constraint precedence, integration ownership, evidence, and stop rules before preserving seed content

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed counts eight local paths as separate evidence even though each archive file is byte-identical to its live-path counterpart, and it assigns all three public links factual status without recording retrieval
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because duplicate detection prevents false corroboration, while role separation prevents a concise quality template from being mistaken for a complete orchestration contract
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: eight paths become eight votes, the implementer report proves completion, the reviewer template defines user authority, or public agent guidance is called current without a complete read
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the map establishes evidence provenance and cannot guarantee current tool semantics, agent availability, or task independence
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add duplicate groups, hashes, role contracts, companion dependencies, platform status, limitations, and promotion gates while retaining all seed rows
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the corpus is a composed protocol, not a pile of prompts: authority comes from role and ordering, not path count

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's local-first thesis does not explain why fresh workers help, when delegation is unsafe, or why specification review must precede quality review
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because context isolation reduces contamination but also removes shared understanding, so explicit task contracts and controller reconciliation are the mechanism that converts isolation into reliability
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: freshness substitutes for context, independent means merely different files, reviewers trust reports, quality polish legitimizes extra scope, or controller abdicates final verification

- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic evidence ordering with a dependency-aware fresh-context, ordered-review, controller-integration thesis

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists generic evidence failures but omits false independence, incomplete task packets, overlapping writers, report trust, reviewer-order inversion, self-review substitution, open findings, and template-over-user precedence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because these failures amplify across workers and can make locally correct artifacts mutually incompatible
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: warnings say communicate better, recovery dispatches more agents, the same reviewer validates itself, or controller edits blindly despite a worker retaining essential context
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry governs orchestration and cannot decide domain correctness without specialist evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three generic rows into a causal dispatch, ownership, review, authority, and integration registry
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that most delegation failures begin as task-model failures before any code is written
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to register hidden dependency, ambiguous ownership, context-starved prompt, assumption without clarification, parallel shared edit, report-only review, spec-quality inversion, reviewer monoculture, unfixed finding, unauthorized commit, and controller abdication
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because these failures amplify across workers and can make locally correct artifacts mutually incompatible
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; warnings say communicate better, recovery dispatches more agents, the same reviewer validates itself, or controller edits blindly despite a worker retaining essential context

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed routes by keywords and omits the source workflow's actual preconditions: a written plan, mostly independent tasks, and same-session execution
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because delegation selected too early converts design uncertainty into multiple inconsistent implementations
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: many tasks imply delegation, different filenames imply independence, same session implies shared understanding, or agent availability becomes permission
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not create agents, branches, commits, or external actions beyond explicit authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace keyword triggering with plan, dependency, ownership, isolation, capability, review, budget, and escalation routing
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the routing decision is itself an architectural decision about information and change ownership
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to confirm a concrete plan, classify dependency and file ownership, identify user permission and workspace isolation, choose same-session delegation only for bounded inspectable tasks, and define review plus integration before dispatch
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because delegation selected too early converts design uncertainty into multiple inconsistent implementations
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; many tasks imply delegation, different filenames imply independence, same session implies shared understanding, or agent availability becomes permission
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: do not create agents, branches, commits, or external actions beyond explicit authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace keyword triggering with plan, dependency, ownership, isolation, capability, review, budget, and escalation routing
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the routing decision is itself an architectural decision about information and change ownership
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the decision record includes objective, plan status, task graph, shared interfaces, owners, isolation, context packet, agent capability, review depth, integration gate, budget, and escalation

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: many tasks imply delegation, different filenames imply independence, same session implies shared understanding, or agent availability becomes permission

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names an agent-system designer but stops before task decomposition, prompt assembly, questions, implementation, ordered reviews, integration, user updates, and recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an end-to-end journey reveals handoff losses and cross-task gaps hidden by per-agent success reports
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: tasks are marked done from reports, the next worker starts with open findings, user changes are not propagated, or final review repeats local tests only
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: adapt the journey to task size and never hide user decisions inside delegation
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the role scenario into the complete plan-to-task-to-review-to-integration lifecycle
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that progress is a sequence of verified state transitions, not a count of dispatched or completed agents
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to read and preserve the full plan, build a dependency and ownership graph, create bounded task packets, dispatch one ready worker, resolve questions, inspect self-review, run spec then quality review loops, integrate, checkpoint, and perform final system review
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because an end-to-end journey reveals handoff losses and cross-task gaps hidden by per-agent success reports
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; tasks are marked done from reports, the next worker starts with open findings, user changes are not propagated, or final review repeats local tests only
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: adapt the journey to task size and never hide user decisions inside delegation
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: extend the role scenario into the complete plan-to-task-to-review-to-integration lifecycle

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table keys Adopt, Adapt, and Avoid to generic local-versus-external evidence agreement instead of task independence, file ownership, review capacity, and user permission
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because adoption criteria tied to observable task properties can be checked before dispatch, while agreement between two document sets says nothing about whether this task can be safely delegated
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adopt is chosen because sources agree, adapt hides an unresolved coupling, avoid becomes a reflex that blocks safe parallel research, or the cost row never names what to undo
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the tradeoff guide ranks same-workspace delegation choices and cannot authorize commits, new agents, or scope the user has not granted
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey each tradeoff row from generic evidence agreement to task independence, ownership clarity, permission state, and review budget
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a tradeoff guide earns its place only when a wrong route leaves a visible trail a reviewer can reverse; routes without undo instructions are gambles, not decisions
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to adopt delegation when the plan is written and tasks are provably independent, adapt it when coupling or missing permissions require serialization or manual slices, and avoid it when design uncertainty or authority gaps dominate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because adoption criteria tied to observable task properties can be checked before dispatch, while agreement between two document sets says nothing about whether this task can be safely delegated
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; adopt is chosen because sources agree, adapt hides an unresolved coupling, avoid becomes a reflex that blocks safe parallel research, or the cost row never names what to undo
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the tradeoff guide ranks same-workspace delegation choices and cannot authorize commits, new agents, or scope the user has not granted
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: rekey each tradeoff row from generic evidence agreement to task independence, ownership clarity, permission state, and review budget
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a tradeoff guide earns its place only when a wrong route leaves a visible trail a reviewer can reverse; routes without undo instructions are gambles, not decisions

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed hierarchy labels the archived skill canonical and its byte-identical live copy merely supporting, labels role templates legacy while they remain the active prompts, and repeats one generic reviewer question for all eight rows
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because byte-identical duplicates cannot carry different authority, and a hierarchy that contradicts observed file equality trains readers to ignore its labels
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: canonical status is read as permission to skip the other templates, legacy labels justify deleting active prompts, duplicate pairs drift after one side is edited, or the repeated question lets every row pass review identically
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy classifies retrieval priority inside this corpus and does not grade external documentation or grant any template orchestration authority
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to regroup rows by duplicate pair and protocol role, align class labels with observed byte equality, and replace the repeated reviewer question with role-specific questions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hierarchy is only meaningful relative to a change process; without a rule for where edits land first, canonical labels decay into historical accidents

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist verifies that sections exist and name things but never asks whether their guidance is correct, consistent across sections, or executable by an agent under real constraints
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because existence checks catch missing prose while the expensive failures are contradictions between sections and gates that cannot actually run, which only content-level checks intercept
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: items are ticked from memory without citations, structural passes are read as content endorsement, or the checklist freezes while sections evolve and silently stops covering new obligations
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist gates this document's readiness for agent use and does not certify the delegation outcomes of tasks that later use it
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to append consistency, executability, authority, and evidence-label items and require cited evidence for every tick
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a checklist that can be completed without reading the document measures the checklist, not the document

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed workload table asserts a one-task, ten-file, three-subtask boundary and truncates its own heading-signal cell mid-word, without deriving any limit from controller attention, review cost, or task coupling
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the binding constraint is controller verification bandwidth, because every dispatched worker returns artifacts that demand line-level review, finding closure, and integration testing that cannot be delegated away
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: worker count is raised because dispatch is cheap, file limits are read as quality guarantees, source-pressure rows are truncated into noise, or workload accounting ignores the re-review loops that dominate real cost
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the workload model bounds one controller session inside one workspace and says nothing about fleet-level scheduling or multi-session pipelines
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rederive each boundary from controller review bandwidth and open-finding limits, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that delegation shifts cost from writing code to verifying it, so any workload model that counts tasks instead of verification effort will overestimate safe capacity
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to size workload by review capacity, dispatching only as many concurrent workers as the controller can spec-review and integrate within the session, which in practice keeps active delegation at one to three bounded tasks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the binding constraint is controller verification bandwidth, because every dispatched worker returns artifacts that demand line-level review, finding closure, and integration testing that cannot be delegated away
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; worker count is raised because dispatch is cheap, file limits are read as quality guarantees, source-pressure rows are truncated into noise, or workload accounting ignores the re-review loops that dominate real cost
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the workload model bounds one controller session inside one workspace and says nothing about fleet-level scheduling or multi-session pipelines
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: rederive each boundary from controller review bandwidth and open-finding limits, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies delegation shifts cost from writing code to verifying it, so any workload model that counts tasks instead of verification effort will overestimate safe capacity
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the model tracks active workers, files under exclusive ownership, open review findings, integration debt, and the context budget spent on task packets
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because the binding constraint is controller verification bandwidth, because every dispatched worker returns artifacts that demand line-level review, finding closure, and integration testing that cannot be delegated away
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where worker count is raised because dispatch is cheap, file limits are read as quality guarantees, source-pressure rows are truncated into noise, or workload accounting ignores the re-review loops that dominate real cost
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the workload model bounds one controller session inside one workspace and says nothing about fleet-level scheduling or multi-session pipelines
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the model tracks active workers, files under exclusive ownership, open review findings, integration debt, and the context budget spent on task packets
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that delegation shifts cost from writing code to verifying it, so any workload model that counts tasks instead of verification effort will overestimate safe capacity
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: worker count is raised because dispatch is cheap, file limits are read as quality guarantees, source-pressure rows are truncated into noise, or workload accounting ignores the re-review loops that dominate real cost
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are three trivially independent subtasks cost less than one hidden-coupled pair, review debt compounds invisibly until integration, and static numeric caps invite gaming instead of judgment
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the model tracks active workers, files under exclusive ownership, open review findings, integration debt, and the context budget spent on task packets
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using the workload model bounds one controller session inside one workspace and says nothing about fleet-level scheduling or multi-session pipelines
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: measure per-run review minutes and set caps empirically, use a work-in-progress limit on open findings instead of worker count, or split oversized efforts into sequential sessions with journal handoffs

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed reliability table promises a 100 percent boundary rate and an 18-of-20 sampled accuracy without any sampling procedure, sample source, or measurement owner ever existing
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because targets create reliability only when someone can actually run the measurement; unmeasurable precision teaches readers to treat all numbers in the file as decoration
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: percentages are quoted as achievements rather than aspirations, samples are drawn only from successful runs, misses trigger no correction, or the zero-unsupported-claim rule quietly exempts the reliability table itself
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the targets judge this document's guidance quality, not the reliability of agent platforms, repositories, or tasks that use it
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to attach a sampling procedure, population, owner, and miss-triggered action to each target and mark all thresholds as unbaselined aspirations

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table

- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed failure table lists source drift, generic advice, context loss, and tool fanout generically but omits the delegation-specific failures its own earlier sections rank highest, such as false task independence and report-trusted review
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because failure tables pay off in the moment of triage, and triage needs the failures that actually occur in this workflow, ranked by blast radius rather than by genericity
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows describe failures too abstractly to match live symptoms, mitigations restate the failure as an imperative, detection lands after integration where evidence is gone, or the table grows without pruning until triage is slower than guessing

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed retry bullets classify failure causes and cap retries sensibly but never define who classifies, where the classification is recorded, or how backpressure releases once gates recover
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retries without recorded classification become infinite loops with amnesia, and dispatch during red gates multiplies unverifiable work faster than the controller can review it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a true contradiction is retried as if transient, backpressure stops work but nothing records why, the halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retry of orchestration steps like dispatch, review, and verification, not application-level retry logic inside the code being written
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add classification ownership, journal recording, and an evidence-based release condition to the existing retry and halt rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure is a memory discipline as much as a flow control, because a halt that does not record its cause converts recoverable congestion into permanent context loss
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify each failure once in the journal, allow a single bounded retry only for transient or stale-evidence causes, halt dispatch while any gate is red, and resume only after the blocking evidence is recorded green
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because retries without recorded classification become infinite loops with amnesia, and dispatch during red gates multiplies unverifiable work faster than the controller can review it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a true contradiction is retried as if transient, backpressure stops work but nothing records why, the halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this governs retry of orchestration steps like dispatch, review, and verification, not application-level retry logic inside the code being written
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add classification ownership, journal recording, and an evidence-based release condition to the existing retry and halt rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure is a memory discipline as much as a flow control, because a halt that does not record its cause converts recoverable congestion into permanent context loss
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the guidance assumes journaled failure records, gates that report red or green unambiguously, one owner per file, and a controller empowered to pause its own dispatch

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: a true contradiction is retried as if transient, backpressure stops work but nothing records why, the halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are transient and systematic failures look identical on first occurrence, retrying a worker with the same prompt reproduces the same blind spot, and paused lanes silently expire context that resumption then rebuilds wrongly
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the guidance assumes journaled failure records, gates that report red or green unambiguously, one owner per file, and a controller empowered to pause its own dispatch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using this governs retry of orchestration steps like dispatch, review, and verification, not application-level retry logic inside the code being written
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: escalate immediately for authority or contradiction failures instead of consuming the retry, re-prompt with amended context rather than replaying, or hand persistent blockers to a fresh session through the journal
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the right retry budget for semantic failures like weak packets is judgment; one bounded retry is a defensible default, not a derived optimum
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: escalate immediately for authority or contradiction failures instead of consuming the retry, re-prompt with amended context rather than replaying, or hand persistent blockers to a fresh session through the journal This changes how the section resolves when a failed delegation step should be retried, escalated, or halted, and how the workflow sheds load when gates go red.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed observability bullets say record sources, commands, latencies, and counters but never state where records live, which journey stage writes them, or who consumes each signal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because evidence captured at the stage that produced it stays accurate and cheap, while end-of-session reconstruction forgets skipped sources and silently flattens the decision path
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: records are written only after success, latency percentiles are quoted for workflows nobody timed, raw transcripts get dumped as audit evidence, or signals accumulate that no reviewer ever consumes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: observability here serves workflow reconstruction and review, not runtime telemetry of shipped software, which belongs to the repository's own monitoring
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to bind each recorded signal to a journey stage, a storage location, and a named consumer, and drop untimed latency claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability that depends on discipline fails under pressure; whatever the workflow does not record automatically will be missing precisely on the runs worth investigating
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to write observations into the lane journal at fixed stages: sources and skips at load, task packets at dispatch, review findings at each gate, and a compact audit block with counters and unresolved risks at completion
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because evidence captured at the stage that produced it stays accurate and cheap, while end-of-session reconstruction forgets skipped sources and silently flattens the decision path
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; records are written only after success, latency percentiles are quoted for workflows nobody timed, raw transcripts get dumped as audit evidence, or signals accumulate that no reviewer ever consumes

- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: bind each recorded signal to a journey stage, a storage location, and a named consumer, and drop untimed latency claims

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed performance method demands latency percentiles and measurement packets while its own pass condition is reviewer comprehension, mixing runtime metrics into a document whose real performance is decision quality
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a reference performs by changing decisions, so its verification must compare decisions made with and against it rather than timing operations it never performs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: percentile theater replaces judgment, pass is declared because a reviewer liked the prose, comparison runs differ in task difficulty so the delta is noise, or the measurement packet is demanded but never collected
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this method evaluates the document's operational usefulness and does not benchmark agent platforms, model quality, or repository build performance
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recenter measurement on decision-quality comparison and restrict latency packets to workflows with actual runtime
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that measuring a document with runtime metrics is a category error that crowds out the harder, more valuable measurement of whether it changes decisions
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to verify performance as decision quality by measuring whether a reader reaches the correct next action, gate, and stop condition faster and with fewer errors than without the reference, reserving latency packets for workflows that actually execute
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a reference performs by changing decisions, so its verification must compare decisions made with and against it rather than timing operations it never performs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; percentile theater replaces judgment, pass is declared because a reviewer liked the prose, comparison runs differ in task difficulty so the delta is noise, or the measurement packet is demanded but never collected
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this method evaluates the document's operational usefulness and does not benchmark agent platforms, model quality, or repository build performance
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: recenter measurement on decision-quality comparison and restrict latency packets to workflows with actual runtime
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies measuring a document with runtime metrics is a category error that crowds out the harder, more valuable measurement of whether it changes decisions
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scale statement names multi-system spans, ownership boundaries, and SLO-bearing traffic as limits but gives no early indicators that a session is approaching them before quality fails
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because scale failures are gradual capacity failures that announce themselves through backlog and rework signals well before the hard boundary, so leading indicators buy the time that hard limits cannot
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: limits are read as targets to approach, splits happen after context is already drifting, merge checkpoints are skipped because parallel writers seem disjoint, or an SLO-bearing change proceeds because no one owned the escalation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the statement bounds this orchestration reference and does not define scaling architecture for the software being built, which needs its own capacity design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add leading approach indicators and pre-crossing actions for each stated boundary
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale limits protect a workflow only when paired with early-warning signals; a boundary detected at the boundary has already been crossed

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed boundary notes define three labels but omit the retrieval-status nuance this file actually needs, where the external URLs are unbrowsed candidates rather than verified facts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because labels earn trust by being checkable, and an external-fact label on an unread URL is exactly the unverifiable claim the labeling system exists to prevent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: external labels imply verification that never happened, inference notes hide which premises they rest on, labels vanish when sections are quoted elsewhere, or a fourth ad hoc label appears and fragments the scheme
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the labels classify evidence provenance in this reference and do not grade the correctness of the underlying sources themselves
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to qualify each label with checkability requirements: paths for local facts, retrieval status for external facts, and named premises for inferences
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that an evidence label is a promise about how a claim can be audited; labels that cannot be audited invert into camouflage for the weakest claims
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep the three-label scheme and qualify it so local facts require a readable path, external labels carry retrieval status and date, and inference notes name which facts they combine so a reader can re-derive them
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because labels earn trust by being checkable, and an external-fact label on an unread URL is exactly the unverifiable claim the labeling system exists to prevent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; external labels imply verification that never happened, inference notes hide which premises they rest on, labels vanish when sections are quoted elsewhere, or a fourth ad hoc label appears and fragments the scheme
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the labels classify evidence provenance in this reference and do not grade the correctness of the underlying sources themselves
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: qualify each label with checkability requirements: paths for local facts, retrieval status for external facts, and named premises for inferences
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies an evidence label is a promise about how a claim can be audited; labels that cannot be audited invert into camouflage for the weakest claims

- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because labels earn trust by being checkable, and an external-fact label on an unread URL is exactly the unverifiable claim the labeling system exists to prevent

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the labels classify evidence provenance in this reference and do not grade the correctness of the underlying sources themselves

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
